< Text>
I haven't shopped at a GameStop in years and after coming in to buy a "new" game I remembered why. This place always has a flea market shadiness feel to it and the employees are trained to make light of any concern you have of its shadiness.

I checked online to see if a game for my son was available at this location. It was, awesome. I headed on over and asked for it. They asked me "new or used?" I wanted a new one since it was on sale and cheaper than their advertised used one. The employee comes back with an opened game and tells me it is new. Two employees are involved now trying to reassure me it is new and the reason it was opened was they had to have a box on display and this was the last one. Of course neither of them realized there was another box on display. They then told me they could shrink wrap it up if I wanted. The booklet inside was a little roughed up and there were fingerprints on the disc. Where else can you go where they push un-boxed, opened media to you and sell it as new? Oh yeah, a flea market. The employees thought there was nothing wrong with this practice which lets me know this is a trained tactic.

Avoid this store and tactics like this, I would recommend going to a big box stores instead. A store with selling ethics like GameStop does not deserve our money. You can always go to a flea market, Craigslist or ebay for used games.</Text>

<Rating>4< /Rating>< text>
Park is accessible from the LA River Walk.  The facilities are fairly new, including flush toilets.  There is a circular dirt track around the park with free exercise equipment.  There are benches and picnic tables and a large grassy area.  There is access to a skate park at one end of the park.  On the other side of the skate park is a park area with a children's playground.  The walk along the river has a two-way bike path in the middle with narrower paths on each side.  There is a walk-in or bike-in entrance to the river walk on Fletcher Drive, just north of Gilroy.  Less than 1/2 mile east of that entrance is access to the larger section of the park.<//text>

<Text>I do not usually write reviews, but my experience with California Moss Control  warrants an exception.

I needed someone to clean the gutters on my two-story home so I entered my contact info into the Home Advisor search engine.  Chris (who I later learned was the owner of Cal.  Moss Control) called me within minutes to schedule an appt for an estimate.

I really didn't understand why a "gutter cleaning" company was called "moss control," but when Chris gave me the estimate he also schooled me on the corrosive effects of the green moss that was growing in my relatively new roof.  It was a form of black mold that feeds on the lye in the composite shingles and that spills off the roof and covers the sidewalk and driveway.  I always thought the green slime we dealt with during the winter was attributed to the northward orientation of our house--not so.  It was digesting my roof and the lye in my aggregate driveway.

So I agreed to hire Chris to clean my gutters, treat my roof and to power wash my sidewalks and driveway.

I cannot overstate how professional and expert he and his crew were.  They treated my property as though it was their own.  And they are environmentally friendly:  Instead of washing everything down the street gutter they opened my sewer and channeled all the effluent into the city sewers.

Yes, I paid for more than a simple gutter cleaning, but every time I walk out front or drive into my driveway I think of how thankful I am for the education Chris gave me.  He saved my expensive roof and ridded me of the green moss I had resigned to live with.  I will definitely use California Moss Control again and will recommend the company highly to all my family and friends!  Thank you Chris!!!!<//Text>< Pictures>
None</Pictures>

< username>
Armando Garcia<//username>
< time>
1550345628283</time>
<Rating>1<//Rating>< Text>
This place was pretty busy, and the older man that we had asked for help was of very little help. He clearly seemed to think he had better things to do than to help us find houseplants that might do well in dimly lit rooms, or to give us some tips on how to help plants live in rooms that are nearly sunless. He seemed bothered by the question and simply recommended we not have plants.

Screw this guy. His attitude amounts to an elitist exclusion of many renters from the privilege of owning some frickin houseplants. I mean, excuse me if there aren't enough huge, sunny remodeled victorians covered in windows to go around for everyone. I get that this place is in Alameda, and Alameda has that entitled "homeowner" vibe, but I presumed nonetheless that a business would be accustomed to questions like mine given that around half of the residents in this part of the east bay are renters. Many of us live in odd conversions or struggle to get some green in given our limited square footage. This is a pretty common set of questions: search the internet for help and you'll find tons of pages that address questions on houseplants in odd spaces. I made my visit here over six months ago and am writing this review because I still find his attitude offensive.

If you have questions about indoor houseplants don't even bother with this place, and if you do, avoid the less cheerful of the two older white men. After some inspiring reading on the internet, I learned that getting some cheap growlights to compensate for low light conditions is one way to go, and my bathroom rainforest is taking shape, no thanks to the curmudgeons at Encinal Nursury.</Text>

In the past the AT&T store on the East edge of West Hollywood would have received 5 Stars hands down but, it has in the past 2 years taken a turn for the worst. YES when my phone got destroyed in an accident they replaced in with a far more durable model but, now getting to talk with the staff and paying your bill on site is difficult. REALLY, anywhere else giving a business money is made easy! In the past they had a much larger variety of phones and tablets to play with to see what you really like. The staff knew just about everything there was in terms to the applications of the devices and, assisted you with how to use your smart phone or tablet features. Now that is not so much the case.

They no longer have at&t Sony Phones or Tablets, a shame because when I got my Sony Xperia Ion (2011) it was by far the best smart phone around in every aspect including durability. The Samsung phones are less capable and, if you drop them out of your pocket on to pavement, you will need a new phone! The new Sony phones have 4K screens and, the most powerful mobile processors but, at&t does not sell them.

Back to customer service, I get the impression that the at&t employees are getting told by management to minimize their interactions with the customers as much as possible. Who came up with this bad idea? This is West Hollywood where being outgoing is an asset! It was a wonderful woman who worked at at&t West Hollywood who showed me how to instantly post pictures in google reviews on the spot with my Sony Xperia Ion, more like her needed.</review>

<userid>103875052594168301115< /userid><username>Donavan Sowell</username><Date>1552347895598</Date><rating>1</rating>< Review>
My review has everything to do with the customer service I received from the sales associate or lack there of. A few positives: The store was clean; and the employees look presentable.

I wanted to port from my carrier to AT&T and told the associate that. He said that I needed two forms of ID (Drivers License and Passport) and a valid major credit card (Not a debit card linked to a bank). Who walks around Los Angeles with 2 forms of ID on them. Also since when do you have to have a Credit Card to get a line of service? I've never heard of anyone having to do that to get service. I had my Drivers License and I even had my American Express and Chase Reserve but I wasn't going home to get a Passport and I have a CA Drivers License. He said "Nope that's the policy. Honestly I felt like it was a bit of "Shopping black judgement; wouldn't be the first time I've had it happen to me!" I told him "Best Buy is across the street I'm just going to go across the street and get the service." He said "That's out policy. I said okay. I walked across the street. I handed Best Buy my Drivers License; they performed my Credit Check. I also opened a Best Buy Credit Card in the process. I got my Iphone XS Max, some Airpods and a screen protecter and the Apple Care and paid for it with my Amx without an issue.

I'm not sure if this is really your policy but if it is; it's counterproductive to how people actually go about life. Nobody carries two forms of ID with them at a given time. If it's not; I would sit down and train your sales associates. You lost  a sale because of it.

I went to the store on Beverly and La Cienega to buy something because it was close to the office and they were super nice. Def will go to that location if I need future assistance.</Review>
